</p><p>With the invention of the airtight pad, and as key technology improved and more keys were added to woodwinds, the need for clarinets in multiple keys was reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_p._25_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_p._25-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> However, the use of multiple instruments in different keys persisted, with the three instruments in C, B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>, and A all used as specified by the composer.
</p><p>The lower-pitched clarinets sound "mellower" (less bright), and the C clarinet—being the highest and therefore brightest of the three—fell out of favour as the other two could cover its range and their sound was considered better.<sup id="cite_ref-longyear_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-longyear-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> While the clarinet in C began to fall out of general use around 1850, some composers continued to write C parts after this date, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Georges_Bizet" title="Georges Bizet">Bizet</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_in_C_(Bizet)" title="Symphony in C (Bizet)">Symphony in C</a> (1855), <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Ilyich_Tchaikovsky" title="Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky">Tchaikovsky</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._2_(Tchaikovsky)" title="Symphony No. 2 (Tchaikovsky)">Symphony No. 2</a> (1872), <a href="/wiki/Bed%C5%99ich_Smetana" title="Bedřich Smetana">Smetana</a>'s overture to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bartered_Bride" title="The Bartered Bride">The Bartered Bride</a></i> (1866) and <i><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1_vlast" title="Má vlast">Má Vlast</a></i> (1874), <a href="/wiki/Anton%C3%ADn_Dvo%C5%99%C3%A1k" title="Antonín Dvořák">Dvořák's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Slavonic_Dances" title="Slavonic Dances">Slavonic Dance</a></i> Op. 46, No. 1 (1878), <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Brahms</a>' <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._4_(Brahms)" title="Symphony No. 4 (Brahms)">Symphony No.&#160;4</a> (1885), <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Mahler" title="Gustav Mahler">Mahler's</a> <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._6_(Mahler)" title="Symphony No. 6 (Mahler)">Symphony No. 6</a> (1906), and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a> deliberately reintroduced it<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to take advantage of its brighter tone, as in <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Rosenkavalier" title="Der Rosenkavalier">Der Rosenkavalier</a></i> (1911).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While technical improvements and an equal-tempered scale reduced the need for two clarinets, the technical difficulty of playing in remote keys persisted, and the A has thus remained a standard orchestral instrument. In addition, by the late 19th century, the orchestral clarinet repertoire contained so much music for clarinet in A that the disuse of this instrument was not practical.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_p._25_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_p._25-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Attempts were made to standardise to the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> instrument between 1930 and 1950 (e.g., tutors recommended learning routine transposition of orchestral A parts on the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet, including solos written for A clarinet, and some manufacturers provided a low E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> on the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> to match the range of the A), but this failed in the orchestral sphere.
</p><p>Similarly there have been E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and D instruments in the upper soprano range, B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>, A, and C instruments in the bass range, and so forth; but over time the E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> instruments have become predominant.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> instrument remains dominant in concert bands and jazz. B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and C instruments are used in some ethnic traditions, such as <a href="/wiki/Klezmer" title="Klezmer">klezmer</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_music">Classical music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarinet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Classical music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, clarinets are part of standard <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">orchestral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Concert_band" title="Concert band">concert band</a> instrumentation.
The orchestra frequently includes two clarinetists playing individual parts—each player is usually equipped with a pair of standard clarinets in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and A, and clarinet parts commonly alternate between B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and A instruments several times over the course of a piece, or less commonly, a movement (e.g., 1st movement <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._3_(Brahms)" title="Symphony No. 3 (Brahms)">Brahms' 3rd symphony</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-anatomy_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anatomy-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Clarinet sections grew larger during the last few decades of the 19th century, often employing a third clarinetist, an E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> or a bass clarinet. In the 20th century, composers such as <a href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky" title="Igor Stravinsky">Igor Stravinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Mahler" title="Gustav Mahler">Gustav Mahler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Messiaen" title="Olivier Messiaen">Olivier Messiaen</a> enlarged the clarinet section on occasion to up to nine players, employing many different clarinets including the E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> or D soprano clarinets, <a href="/wiki/Basset-horn" class="mw-redirect" title="Basset-horn">basset horn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alto_clarinet" title="Alto clarinet">alto clarinet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bass_clarinet" title="Bass clarinet">bass clarinet</a>, and/or <a href="/wiki/Contrabass_clarinet" title="Contrabass clarinet">contrabass clarinet</a>.
</p><p>In concert bands, clarinets are an important part of the instrumentation. The E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet, B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet, alto clarinet, bass clarinet, and contra-alto/contrabass clarinet are commonly used in concert bands. Concert bands generally have multiple B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets; there are commonly 3 B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet parts with 2–3 players per part. There is generally only one player per part on the other clarinets. There are not always E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet, alto clarinet, and contra-alto clarinets/contrabass clarinet parts in concert band music, but all three are quite common.
</p>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Contrabass_Clarinet_-_Fragment_from_%27Late_Spring%27.ogg" title="File:Contrabass Clarinet - Fragment from &#39;Late Spring&#39;.ogg">Tudor Tulok – Fragment from 'Late Spring'</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="21.57566893424" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Contrabass_Clarinet_-_Fragment_from_&#39;Late_Spring&#39;.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/02/Contrabass_Clarinet_-_Fragment_from_%27Late_Spring%27.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (172 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="171591" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/0/02/Contrabass_Clarinet_-_Fragment_from_%27Late_Spring%27.ogg/Contrabass_Clarinet_-_Fragment_from_%27Late_Spring%27.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="203048" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"></div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>This practice of using a variety of clarinets to achieve coloristic variety was common in <a href="/wiki/20th-century_classical_music" title="20th-century classical music">20th-century classical music</a> and continues today. However, many clarinetists and conductors prefer to play parts originally written for obscure instruments on B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> or E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets, which are often of better quality and more prevalent and accessible.<sup id="cite_ref-anatomy_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anatomy-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The clarinet is widely used as a solo instrument. The relatively late evolution of the clarinet (when compared to other orchestral woodwinds) has left solo repertoire from the <a href="/wiki/Classical_music_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical music era">Classical</a> period and later, but few works from the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_concerto" title="Clarinet concerto">clarinet concertos</a> have been written to showcase the instrument, with the concerti by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Copland" title="Aaron Copland">Copland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Maria_von_Weber" title="Carl Maria von Weber">Weber</a> being well known.
</p><p>Many works of <a href="/wiki/Chamber_music" title="Chamber music">chamber music</a> have also been written for the clarinet. Common combinations are:
</p>
<div>
<ul><li>Clarinet and piano (including <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_sonata" title="Clarinet sonata">clarinet sonatas</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_trio" title="Clarinet trio">Clarinet trio</a>; Clarinet, piano, and another instrument (for example, <a href="/wiki/String_instrument" title="String instrument">string instrument</a> or voice)<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_choir" title="Clarinet choir">Clarinet quartet</a>: three B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets and <a href="/wiki/Bass_clarinet" title="Bass clarinet">bass clarinet</a>; two B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets, <a href="/wiki/Alto_clarinet" title="Alto clarinet">alto clarinet</a>, and bass; and other possibilities such as the use of a <a href="/wiki/Basset_horn" title="Basset horn">basset horn</a>, especially in European classical works.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lawson1995_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson1995-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_quintet" title="Clarinet quintet">Clarinet quintet</a>, generally made up of a clarinet plus a <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reed_quintet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reed quintet (page does not exist)">Reed quintet</a>, consists of oboe (doubling <a href="/wiki/English_horn" class="mw-redirect" title="English horn">English horn</a>), clarinet, <a href="/wiki/Alto_saxophone" title="Alto saxophone">alto saxophone</a> (doubling <a href="/wiki/Soprano_saxophone" title="Soprano saxophone">soprano saxophone</a>), bass clarinet, and bassoon.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wind_quintet" title="Wind quintet">Wind quintet</a>, consists of flute, oboe, clarinet, bassoon, and <a href="/wiki/French_horn" title="French horn">horn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trio_d%27anches&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trio d&#39;anches (page does not exist)">Trio d'anches</a>, or <i>trio of reeds</i> consists of oboe, clarinet, and bassoon.<sup id="cite_ref-costa_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costa-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wind_octet" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind octet">Wind octet</a>, consists of pairs of oboes, clarinets, bassoons, and horns.<sup id="cite_ref-costa_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costa-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tbody><tr><td></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jazz">Jazz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarinet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Jazz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG/220px-Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG/330px-Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG/440px-Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="742" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pete_Fountain_1962.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jazz clarinetist Pete Fountain</div></div></div>
<p>The clarinet was originally a central instrument in jazz, beginning with the New Orleans players in the 1910s. It remained a signature instrument of jazz music through much of the <a href="/wiki/Big_band" title="Big band">big band</a> era into the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> American players <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Picou" title="Alphonse Picou">Alphonse Picou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Shields" title="Larry Shields">Larry Shields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Noone" title="Jimmie Noone">Jimmie Noone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Dodds" title="Johnny Dodds">Johnny Dodds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Bechet" title="Sidney Bechet">Sidney Bechet</a> were all pioneers of the instrument in jazz. The B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> soprano was the most common instrument, but a few early jazz musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Louis_Nelson_Delisle" title="Louis Nelson Delisle">Louis Nelson Delisle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcide_Nunez" title="Alcide Nunez">Alcide Nunez</a> preferred the C soprano, and many New Orleans jazz brass bands have used E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> soprano.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Swing clarinetists such as <a href="/wiki/Benny_Goodman" title="Benny Goodman">Benny Goodman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artie_Shaw" title="Artie Shaw">Artie Shaw</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Woody_Herman" title="Woody Herman">Woody Herman</a> led successful big bands and smaller groups from the 1930s onward.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ellington" title="Duke Ellington">Duke Ellington</a>, active from the 1920s to the 1970s, used the clarinet as lead instrument in his works, with several players of the instrument (<a href="/wiki/Barney_Bigard" title="Barney Bigard">Barney Bigard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Hamilton" title="Jimmy Hamilton">Jimmy Hamilton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Procope" title="Russell Procope">Russell Procope</a>) spending a significant portion of their careers in his orchestra. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Carney" title="Harry Carney">Harry Carney</a>, primarily Ellington's baritone saxophonist, occasionally doubled on bass clarinet. Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Pee_Wee_Russell" title="Pee Wee Russell">Pee Wee Russell</a> had a long and successful career in small groups.
</p><p>With the decline of the big bands' popularity in the late 1940s, the clarinet faded from its prominent position in jazz. By that time, an interest in <a href="/wiki/Dixieland" title="Dixieland">Dixieland</a> or traditional New Orleans jazz had revived; <a href="/wiki/Pete_Fountain" title="Pete Fountain">Pete Fountain</a> was one of the best known performers in this genre.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wilber" title="Bob Wilber">Bob Wilber</a>, active since the 1950s, is a more eclectic jazz clarinetist, playing in several classic jazz styles.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> During the 1950s and 1960s, Britain underwent a surge in the popularity of what was termed 'Trad jazz'. In 1956 the British clarinetist <a href="/wiki/Acker_Bilk" title="Acker Bilk">Acker Bilk</a> founded his own ensemble.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Several singles recorded by Bilk reached the British pop charts, including the ballad "<a href="/wiki/Stranger_on_the_Shore" title="Stranger on the Shore">Stranger on the Shore</a>".
</p><p>The clarinet's place in the jazz ensemble was usurped by the <a href="/wiki/Saxophone" title="Saxophone">saxophone</a>, which projects a more powerful sound and uses a less complicated fingering system.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The requirement for an increased speed of execution in modern jazz also did not favour the clarinet, but the clarinet did not entirely disappear. The clarinetist <a href="/wiki/Stan_Hasselg%C3%A5rd" title="Stan Hasselgård">Stan Hasselgård</a> made a transition from swing to bebop in the mid-1940s.  A few players such as <a href="/wiki/Buddy_DeFranco" title="Buddy DeFranco">Buddy DeFranco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott_(musician)" title="Tony Scott (musician)">Tony Scott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Giuffre" title="Jimmy Giuffre">Jimmy Giuffre</a> emerged during the 1950s playing <a href="/wiki/Bebop" title="Bebop">bebop</a> or other styles. A little later, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Dolphy" title="Eric Dolphy">Eric Dolphy</a> (on bass clarinet), <a href="/wiki/Perry_Robinson" title="Perry Robinson">Perry Robinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Carter_(jazz_musician)" title="John Carter (jazz musician)">John Carter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theo_J%C3%B6rgensmann" title="Theo Jörgensmann">Theo Jörgensmann</a>, and others used the clarinet in <a href="/wiki/Free_jazz" title="Free jazz">free jazz</a>. The French composer and clarinetist <a href="/wiki/Jean-Christian_Michel" title="Jean-Christian Michel">Jean-Christian Michel</a> initiated a jazz-classical cross-over on the clarinet with the drummer <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Clarke" title="Kenny Clarke">Kenny Clarke</a>.
</p><p>In the U.S., the prominent players on the instrument since the 1980s have included <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Daniels" title="Eddie Daniels">Eddie Daniels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Byron" title="Don Byron">Don Byron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marty_Ehrlich" title="Marty Ehrlich">Marty Ehrlich</a>, and others playing the clarinet in more contemporary contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_genres">Other genres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarinet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other genres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The clarinet is uncommon, but not unheard of, in <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock music</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Martini" title="Jerry Martini">Jerry Martini</a> played clarinet on <a href="/wiki/Sly_and_the_Family_Stone" title="Sly and the Family Stone">Sly and the Family Stone</a>'s 1968 hit, "Dance to the Music"; <a href="/wiki/Don_Byron" title="Don Byron">Don Byron</a>, a founder of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Rock_Coalition" title="Black Rock Coalition">Black Rock Coalition</a> who was a member of hard rock guitarist <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Reid" title="Vernon Reid">Vernon Reid</a>'s band, plays clarinet on the <i>Mistaken Identity</i> album (1996). <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Waits" title="Tom Waits">Tom Waits</a> have also all used clarinet on occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> A clarinet is prominently featured for two different solos in <a href="/wiki/Breakfast_in_America_(song)" title="Breakfast in America (song)">Breakfast in America</a>, the title song from the <a href="/wiki/Supertramp" title="Supertramp">Supertramp</a> album of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Clarinets feature prominently in <a href="/wiki/Klezmer" title="Klezmer">klezmer</a> music, which entails a distinctive style of playing.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The use of quarter-tones requires a different embouchure.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Some klezmer musicians prefer Albert system clarinets.<sup id="cite_ref-hoeprich_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoeprich-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The popular <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> music styles of <a href="/wiki/Choro" title="Choro">choro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samba_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Samba (music)">samba</a> use the clarinet.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Prominent contemporary players include Paulo Moura, Naylor 'Proveta' Azevedo, Paulo Sérgio dos Santos, and Cuban born <a href="/wiki/Paquito_D%27Rivera" title="Paquito D&#39;Rivera">Paquito D'Rivera</a>.
</p><p>Even though it has been adopted recently in Albanian folklore (around the 18th century), the clarinet, or <i>gërneta</i> as it is called, is one of the most important instruments in Albania, especially in the central and southern areas.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The clarinet plays a crucial role in <i>saze</i> (folk) ensembles that perform in weddings and other celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> It is worth mentioning that the <i>kaba</i> (an instrumental Albanian Isopolyphony included in UNESCO's intangible cultural heritage list<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>) is characteristic of these ensembles.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Prominent Albanian clarinet players include Selim Leskoviku, Gaqo Lena, Remzi Lela (Çobani), Laver Bariu (Ustai), and Nevruz Nure (Lulushi i Korçës).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The clarinet is prominent in Bulgarian wedding music also; it is an offshoot of Roma/Romani traditional music.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Papazov" title="Ivo Papazov">Ivo Papazov</a> is a well-known clarinetist in this genre. In <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravian</a> <a href="/wiki/Hammered_dulcimer" title="Hammered dulcimer">dulcimer</a> bands, the clarinet is usually the only wind instrument among string instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In old-town folk music in <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> (called <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Calgija" title="Čalgija">čalgija</a> ("чалгија")), the clarinet has the most important role in wedding music; clarinet solos mark the high point of dancing euphoria.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> One of the most renowned Macedonian clarinet players is <a href="/wiki/Tale_Ognenovski" title="Tale Ognenovski">Tale Ognenovski</a>, who gained worldwide fame for his virtuosity.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, the clarinet (usually referred to as "κλαρίνο"—"clarino") is prominent in traditional music, especially in central, northwest, and northern Greece (<a href="/wiki/Thessaly" title="Thessaly">Thessaly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epirus_(region)" title="Epirus (region)">Epirus</a>, and Macedonia).<sup id="cite_ref-pappas_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pappas-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The double-reed <a href="/wiki/Zurna" title="Zurna">zurna</a> was the dominant woodwind instrument before the clarinet arrived in the country, although many Greeks regard the clarinet as a native instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-hoeprich_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoeprich-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Traditional dance music, wedding music, and laments include a clarinet soloist and quite often improvisations.<sup id="cite_ref-pappas_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pappas-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Petroloukas Chalkias is a famous clarinetist in this genre.
</p><p>The instrument is equally famous in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, especially the lower-pitched clarinet in G. The western European clarinet crossed via Turkey to <a href="/wiki/Arabic_music" title="Arabic music">Arabic music</a>, where it is widely used in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_pop" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic pop">Arabic pop</a>, especially if the intention of the arranger is to imitate the Turkish style.<sup id="cite_ref-hoeprich_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoeprich-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_Clarinet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Turkish_Clarinet.jpg/500px-Turkish_Clarinet.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/Turkish_Clarinet.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_Clarinet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Turkish clarinet</div></div></div></div>
<p>Also in Turkish <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a>, a clarinet-like woodwind instrument, the <a href="/wiki/Sipsi" title="Sipsi">sipsi</a>, is used. However, it is far more rare than the soprano clarinet and is mainly limited to folk music of the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Region" title="Aegean Region">Aegean Region</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Groups_of_clarinets">Groups of clarinets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarinet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Groups of clarinets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Groups of clarinets playing together have become increasingly popular among clarinet enthusiasts in recent years. Common forms are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_choir" title="Clarinet choir">Clarinet choir</a>, which features a large number of clarinets playing together, usually involves a range of different members of the clarinet family (see <a href="/wiki/Clarinet#Extended_family_of_clarinets" title="Clarinet">Extended family of clarinets</a>). The homogeneity of tone across the different members of the clarinet family produces an effect with some similarities to a human <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Clarinet quartet, usually three B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> sopranos and one B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> bass, or two B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>, an E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> alto clarinet, and a B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> bass clarinet, or sometimes four B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> sopranos.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Clarinet choirs and quartets often play arrangements of both classical and popular music, in addition to a body of literature specially written for a combination of clarinets by composers such as <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Cooke" title="Arnold Cooke">Arnold Cooke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Uhl" title="Alfred Uhl">Alfred Uhl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Caillet" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucien Caillet">Lucien Caillet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Nelh%C3%BDbel" title="Václav Nelhýbel">Václav Nelhýbel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extended_family_of_clarinets">Extended family of clarinets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarinet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Extended family of clarinets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_family" title="Clarinet family">Clarinet family</a></div>
<p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Family_(musical_instruments)" title="Family (musical instruments)">family</a> of many differently pitched clarinet types, some of which are very rare. The following are the most important sizes, from highest to lowest:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Klarinetten_von_Herbert_Wurlitzer_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Klarinetten_von_Herbert_Wurlitzer_2.jpg/290px-Klarinetten_von_Herbert_Wurlitzer_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="531" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Klarinetten_von_Herbert_Wurlitzer_2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="356" data-file-height="652" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Klarinetten_von_Herbert_Wurlitzer_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bass_clarinet" title="Bass clarinet">Bass clarinet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basset_horn" title="Basset horn">Basset horn</a>, clarinets in D, B♭, A, high G and E♭</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg/290px-Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="435" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg/435px-Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg/580px-Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="1660" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarinette_metal_CAlt_CBas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Contrabass and contra-alto clarinets</div></div></div>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>Name</th>
<th>Key</th>
<th>Commentary</th>
<th>Range (concert)
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Piccolo_clarinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Piccolo clarinet">Piccolo clarinet</a>
</td>
<td>A<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>
</td>
<td>Now rare, used for Italian military music and some contemporary pieces for its sonority.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop Ab reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="76" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Clar_sop_Ab_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="155" data-file-height="118" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/E-flat_clarinet" title="E-flat clarinet">E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet</a>
<p>(Sopranino clarinet in E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>)
</p>
</td>
<td>E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>
</td>
<td>It has a characteristically shrill timbre, and is used to great effect in the classical orchestra whenever a brighter, or sometimes a more rustic or comical sound is called for. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a> featured it as a solo instrument in his <a href="/wiki/Symphonic_poem" title="Symphonic poem">symphonic poem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Till_Eulenspiegel" title="Till Eulenspiegel">Till Eulenspiegel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tschaikov_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tschaikov-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> It is much used in the <a href="/wiki/Concert_band" title="Concert band">concert band</a> repertoire where it helps out the <a href="/wiki/Piccolo_flute" class="mw-redirect" title="Piccolo flute">piccolo flute</a> in the higher register and is very compatible with other band instruments, especially those in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop Eb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="74" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5a/Clar_sop_Eb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="162" data-file-height="120" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/D_clarinet" class="mw-redirect" title="D clarinet">D clarinet</a>
<p>(Sopranino clarinet in D)
</p>
</td>
<td>D
</td>
<td>This was, to the high pitched E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> instrument, what the A clarinet is to the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>. Advances in playing technique and the instrument's mechanism meant that players could play parts for the D instrument on their E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> thus making this instrument more and more expendable. Though a few early pieces were written for it, its repertoire is now very limited in Western music. Nonetheless <a href="/wiki/Stravinsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Stravinsky">Stravinsky</a> included both the D and E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets in his instrumentation for <a href="/wiki/The_Rite_Of_Spring" class="mw-redirect" title="The Rite Of Spring">The Rite Of Spring</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tschaikov_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tschaikov-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop D reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="80" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/Clar_sop_D_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="128" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Soprano_clarinet" title="Soprano clarinet">C clarinet</a>
<p>(Soprano clarinet in C)
</p>
</td>
<td>C
</td>
<td>Although this clarinet was very common in the instrument's earliest period, its use began to dwindle, and by the second decade of the twentieth century it had become practically obsolete and disappeared from the orchestra. From the time of Mozart, many composers began to favour the mellower, lower pitched instruments, and the timbre of the 'C' instrument may have been considered too bright.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Also, to avoid having to carry an extra instrument that required another reed and mouthpiece, orchestral players preferred to play parts for this instrument on their B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinets, transposing up a tone.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> It is enjoying a resurgence in popular musical styles such as Klezmer, as an instrument in schools and in more historically accurate interpretations of the classical and Romantic repertoire such as the First and Fifth Symphonies of <a href="/wiki/Beethoven" class="mw-redirect" title="Beethoven">Beethoven</a>.
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop C reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="76" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/Clar_sop_C_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="119" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_family" title="Clarinet family">B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet</a>
<p>(Soprano clarinet in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>)
</p>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/B%E2%99%AD_(musical_note)" title="B♭ (musical note)">B♭</a>
</td>
<td>The most common type: used in most styles of music.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Usually the term <i>clarinet</i> on its own refers to this instrument. It was commonly used in early <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swing_music" title="Swing music">swing</a>. This was the instrument of renowned and popular figures such as <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Bechet" title="Sidney Bechet">Sidney Bechet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benny_Goodman" title="Benny Goodman">Benny Goodman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woody_Herman" title="Woody Herman">Woody Herman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Artie_Shaw" title="Artie Shaw">Artie Shaw</a>.
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop Bb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="79" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Clar_sop_Bb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="124" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Clarinet_family" title="Clarinet family">'A' clarinet</a>
<p>(Soprano clarinet in A)
</p>
</td>
<td>A
</td>
<td>Many clarinetists and some composers maintain that this has a somewhat mellower sound than the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>; most people can't perceive a difference in blindfold testing. It is frequently used in orchestral and chamber music, especially of the nineteenth century. The <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_Quintet_(Brahms)" title="Clarinet Quintet (Brahms)">Clarinet Quintet by Brahms (op. 115)</a> is a notable example.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar sop A reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="78" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/62/Clar_sop_A_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="153" data-file-height="119" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Basset_clarinet" title="Basset clarinet">Basset clarinet</a>
</td>
<td>A
</td>
<td>Clarinet in A extended to a low C; used primarily to play Classical-era music.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Mozart's Clarinet Concerto was written for this instrument, though it is frequently played in a version for the ordinary A clarinet. Basset clarinets in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> also exist; this instrument is required to play the obbligato to the aria "Parto, parto" in Mozart's La Clemenza di Tito.
</td>
<td>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Basset-horn" class="mw-redirect" title="Basset-horn">Basset-horn</a>
</td>
<td>F
</td>
<td>Similar in appearance to the alto, but differs in that it is pitched in F, has an extended range to low C, and has a narrower bore on most models. Mozart's Clarinet Concerto was originally sketched out as a concerto for basset horn in G. Rarely used today.
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Cor basset F reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG/100px-Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="73" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG/150px-Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Cor_basset_F_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="164" data-file-height="119" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Alto_clarinet" title="Alto clarinet">Alto clarinet</a>
</td>
<td>E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> or F
</td>
<td>Sometimes referred to (mostly in Europe) as the <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> clarinet. Its greater size and consequently lower pitch give it a rich, dark sonority capable of greater resonance than the soprano instruments, but with less projection than the larger <a href="/wiki/Bass_clarinet" title="Bass clarinet">bass clarinet</a>. It is used in chamber music and concert bands, and occasionally, if rarely, in orchestras.  A few players have specialized in using the alto in jazz (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Gianluigi_Trovesi" title="Gianluigi Trovesi">Gianluigi Trovesi</a>).  The alto in F is considered obsolete.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar alto Eb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="84" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/89/Clar_alto_Eb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="158" data-file-height="133" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bass_clarinet" title="Bass clarinet">Bass clarinet</a>
</td>
<td>B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> or A
</td>
<td>Invented in the 1770s, it only became popular around a hundred years later when it contributed to the rich orchestral palettes of composers such as <a href="/wiki/Wagner" class="mw-redirect" title="Wagner">Wagner</a> and the late <a href="/wiki/Romantics" class="mw-redirect" title="Romantics">Romantics</a>. It has become a mainstay of the modern orchestra. Originally, the third clarinet would double on bass, but now, most orchestras employ a specialist devoted principally to this instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It is used in concert bands, contemporary music, and enjoys, along with the B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> clarinet, a considerable role in jazz. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Dolphy" title="Eric Dolphy">Eric Dolphy</a> was one of its more remarkable exponents.  The bass clarinet in A, which had a vogue among certain composers from the mid-19th to the mid-20th centuries, is now so rare as to usually be considered obsolete.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar bas Bb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="70" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Clar_bas_Bb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="168" data-file-height="117" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Contra-alto_clarinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Contra-alto clarinet">E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> contrabass clarinet</a> (also called Contraalto clarinet)
</td>
<td>EE<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>
</td>
<td>Used in clarinet choirs and is common in concert bands.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar ctalto Eb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="76" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Clar_ctalto_Eb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="173" data-file-height="131" /></a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Contrabass_clarinet" title="Contrabass clarinet">Contrabass clarinet</a> (also called B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> subcontrabass or double-bass clarinet)
</td>
<td>BB<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span>
</td>
<td>Used in clarinet choirs and is common in concert bands. It is sometimes used in orchestras. <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schoenberg" title="Arnold Schoenberg">Arnold Schoenberg</a> calls for one in his <a href="/wiki/Five_Pieces_for_Orchestra" title="Five Pieces for Orchestra">Five Pieces for Orchestra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_73-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Clar ctbas Bb reel.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG/100px-Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="68" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG/150px-Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Clar_ctbas_Bb_reel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="192" data-file-height="130" /></a>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>EEE<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> and BBB<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Subcontrabass_clarinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcontrabass clarinet">octocontra-alto and octocontrabass</a> clarinets have also been built.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> There have also been soprano clarinets in C, A, and B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> with curved barrels and bells marketed under the names <a href="/wiki/Saxonette" title="Saxonette">saxonette</a>, claribel, and clariphon.
</p>
